Criteria and Procedure for Fellowship Award
1.        Objective.  The fellowship program has been designed to build up
the technical, administrative or managerial capabilities of MEN staff, to
allow them to implement the project efficiently, formulate sound plans for
future sector development and execute these plans in a cost-effective
manner.
2.        Criteria for Fellowships Awards
(a)  Field of study:  Fellowships would be awarded only for studies
related to project activities or future professional responsi-
bilities in MEN;
(b)  Qualifications:  Candidates must:
(i)  have the requisite academic background;
(ii)  have minimum of one year of work experience in MEN;
(iii) have fluency in the language of course of study;
(iv)  be in good health;
(v)  demonstrate intellectual curiosity, analytical capability,
initiative, drive as well as the ability to work in a team
and share knowledge with others; and
(vi)  manifest potential for advancement.
(c) Other criteria: Candidates must:
(i)  have a good understanding of MEN's medium- and long-term
strategy, as well as of the project, its objectives and
implementation;
(ii)  agree to serve MEN for at least three years in the area for
which he/she is awarded the fellowship; and
(iii) repay all expenses incurred in pre?aration for and during
his/her fellowship training, should he/she decide to drop
out of the program or elect not to serve in MEN.
3.        Procedure for Fellowships Award and Management.  Candidates for
fellowships would be proposed by the relevant project Directorates.
Selection would oe made by a panel chaired by the Project Coordinator and
including the Secretary General and representatives from the Directorates
General of Education and of Administration/Finance. The fellowship
recipient would sign with MEN an agreement identifying the post for which
he/she would be trained and specifying the obligations of each party
(especially para. 2. (c) (iii) above).



- 171 -            ANNEX 3-15
Page 1 of 3
CENTRAL AFRICAN REPUBLIC
EDUCATION REHABILITATION AND DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
PROCUREMENT PROCEDURES
Part A. Procurement of Goods and Works
1.      Except as provided in Part C hereof, goods and woags shall be
procured under contracts awarded in accordance with procedures consistent
with those set forth in Sections 1 and II of the "Guidelinrq for Procure-
ment Under IBRD Loans and IDA Credits" published by the Bank in May 1985
(the guidelines).
2.      Bidders for the works for remodeling administration buildings and
for school construction shall be prequalified as described in paragraph
2.10 of the guidelines.
Part B. Preference for Domestic Manufacturers
3.      In the procurement of goods in accordance with the procedures
described in Part A. 1 hereof, goods manufactured in CAR may be granted a
margin of prefere'nce of 15% in accordance with, and subject to, the
provisions of paragraphs 2.55 and 2.56 of the guidelines and paragraphs 1
through 4 of Appendix 2 thereto.
Part C. Preference for Domestic Contractors
4.      In the procurement of works in accordance with the procedures
eescribed in Part 1 hereof, the Borrower may grant a margin of preference
of 7.5% to domestic contractors in accordance with, and subject to the
provisions of paragraphs 2.55 and 2.56 of the guidelines and paragraph 5 of
Appendix 2 thereto.
Part D. Other Procurement Procedures
5.      Equipmen; (excluding printing of textbooks) and furniture con-
tracts as well as building materials and construction contracts estimated
to cost the equivalent of between US$20,000 and US$100,000 equivalent per
contract, which are not likely to attract overseas foreign firms, would be
procured under contracts awarded on the basis of competitive bidding,
advertised locally (LCB), in accordance with procedures satisfactory to the
Association, provided the aggregate amount of such procurement shall not
exceed the equivalent of US$2.65 million equivalent.
6.      Items that cannot be grouped into bid packages of at least
US$20,000 equivalent provided the aggregate amount of such procurement
shall not exceed US$190,000 equivalent, would be procured under contracts
awarded on the basis of at least three suppliers or contractors eligible
under the guidelines, in accordance with procedures acceptable to the
Association.



- 172 -
ANNEX 3-15
Page 2 of 3
Part E. Review by the Bank of Procurement Decisions
1. Prior Review
7.      For all contracts or bid packages of at least US$100,000 equiva-
lent, each of the following stages in the procurement process would be
subject to IDA's prior review and commented upon by IDA staff before they
are implemented and finalized:
- Advertisement
Prequalification (if called for)
- Bidding documents and addenda
- Bid evaluation and proposal for award of contract
- Contract documents
- Subsequent major modifications of the contract
2. Initial Review
8.      For all contracts valued at up to US$100,000 equivalent, an
initial review, followed by a post review or a random review depending on
size of contract, by IDA staff would be required for standard documents
which are common to a number of procurement operations, for example:
- the general format of advertisements and their circulation;
- the prequalification questionnaire and method of evaluation;
- standard reg .sters of prequalified contractors; and
- standard bidding documents, including instruction to bidders,
general conditions of contract, and in some instances, technical
specifications.
3. Post Review
9.      For all contracts or bid packages estimated at between US$20,000
and US$100,000 equivalent, two copies of the final contracts, together with
the bidding documents, bid evaluation and award decision, would be
'1irnished to IDA for post review before the first application for with-
drawal of credit funds against these contracts.
Random Review
10.     The provisions of the preceding subparagraphs of Part E, (1), (2)
and (3) shall not apply to contracts valued at under US$20,000 equivalent
on account of which the Bank has authorized withdrawals from the Credit
Account on the basis of statements of expenditure. Such contracts shall be
retained at the Project Coordination Unit for random review by IDA super-
vision missions and for regular semi-annual audits.
Part F. Specialist Services and Fellowships/Local Training
11.     Specialist services, including audit se.vices, valued at US$5.0
mrillion equivalent, would be contracted in accordance with IDA's guidelines
and on the basis of invitation for proposals from three to six qualified
and experienced consultant firms and agencies and on an exceptional basis,
kfrom individual specialists. Fellowships, valued at US$590,000 equivalent,



- 173 -           ANNEX 3-15
Page 3 of 3
would be contracted in accordance with IDA's guidelines. Local training
represents US$2.59 million equivalent and would be carried out under
principles and procedures satisfactory to the Bank. Services of trainers
are covered under specialist services.
Part G. Consumables
12.     Consumables (office supply, spare parts, gasoline, other consum-
ables), would be procured through LCB according to procedures acceptable to
IDA. All goods or services would be grouped, wherever possible, into bid
packages of at least US$20,000 equivalent.
Part H. Participation by ForeiEn Firms
13.     About 57% of the contracts for works and goods would be procured
through LCB according to procedures acceptable to IDA; if foreign firms
wish to participate under these circumstances, they would be allowed to do
so in accordance with local procedures.
Part I.
14.     The figure of 5% would be specified for purposes of paragraph h
of Appendix 1 to the guidelines (related to any material modification or
waiver of the terms and conditions of contracts or granting a material
extension of the stipulated time, or issuing any change order under such
contract which would increase the cost of contracts by more than 5% of the
original price).

ANNEX 3-16
CENTRAL AFRICAN REPUBLIC
EDUCATION REHABILITATION AND DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
SUMMARY OF GOVERNMENT AND LOCAL COMMUNITIES CONTRIBUTIONS
1.       The Government's financial contribution to che project is
estimated at CFAF 391,847,000, equivalent to US$1,343,000 or 6% of the
total project cost. The Government's contribution would finance, on an
increasing basis, an average of 30% of the incremental operating costs and
the totality of the primary school directors' housing.l/
2.       The local communities' contribution, generated from parents
associations (APEs), is estimated at CFAF 360,044,000, equivalent to
US$1,234,000 or 6% of the total project cost. The APEs would finance
either in kind (labor, and local building materials) or through cash
contributions, the completion of the classroom structure with locally made
blocks (artisanal bricks or blocks of stabilized earth compacted in
hand-operated presses) the school sanitary facilities and the fencing.
3.       The table below shows the breakdown of the Government and local
community contribution by expenditure category and calendar year.
Government and Local Contributions by Exependiture and Catexory and Calendar Year
